    "content": "# Top data breaches of February 2026 (so far) (updated daily) - SharkStriker\n## February 2026 Data Breaches (So Far)\n02 Feb 2026\n![](https://sharkstriker.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Top-data-breaches-of-February-2026-so-far-updated-daily.jpg)\n## Top data breaches of February 2026\n2026 began with some of the biggest and most impactful data breaches that have costed organizations days of operations, terabytes of data, and years of reputation.\nAttackers have become more advanced with their techniques using AI to drive more stealthy and automated attacks that target sensitive information assets by exploiting hidden unaddressed weaknesses and awareness gaps.\nLet us take a closer look at some of the top data breaches of February 2026.\n## Top data breaches of January 2026\n### Victim: Denton Municipal Utilities\n#### About\nThe Denton Utilities is a water, wastewater, and drainage service provider based in Denton, Texas, offering online services for the payment of utility bills.\n#### Industry\nPublic sector\n#### What happened?\nBridgePay, a payment vendor for Denton Utility, became a target of a cyber attack, causing disruption of its (Denton Utility’s) bill payment services.\n#### Impact\nThe ransomware attack caused massive disruption in bill payment services and may have compromised the data of its customers.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: European Commission\n#### About\nThe European Commission is the European Union’s primary executive body operating as the cabinet government.\n#### Industry\nPublic sector\n#### What happened?\nThe European Commission’s central infrastructure identified signs of a cyber attack. Within 9 hours, the incident was contained.\n#### Impact\nThe European Commission reported on 30th January that the cyber attack may have compromised its staff’s personal data, including their names and mobile numbers.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: DAF Directorate of File Automation (DAF) Senegal\n#### About\nThe Directorate of File Automation (DAF) is Senegal’s government agency responsible for managing the identification documents, including ID cards, biometric records, passports, and electoral data.\n#### Industry\nPublic sector\n#### What happened?\nThe DAF became a victim of a cyber attack, causing massive disruption in operations and a temporary suspension of production.\n#### Impact\nThe attack compromised 139 TB of data, including the citizen database, biometric data, immigration records, and backup systems. It also caused a massive disruption in operations for five days and the suspension of production.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: Terry Reilly Health Services\n#### About\nTerry Reilly is a Treasure Valley-based healthcare services provider that offers affordable and accessible comprehensive healthcare services to its residents.\n#### Industry\nHealthcare\n#### What happened?\nTerry Reilly discovered that its third-party vendor has become a victim of a cyber attack.\n#### Impact\nThe data breach has compromised data belonging to patients, including their personal information, including names, birthdates, health insurance numbers, insurer information, and personal health and insurance records.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: Japan Airlines\n#### About\nJapan Airlines is one of the biggest airlines in Japan and is part of the JAL group of companies. It was founded in 1951 as a government-owned business and became Japan’s national airline in 1953.\n#### Industry\nAirlines\n#### What happened?\nJapan Airlines discovered unauthorized access to its systems and data on 9th February 2026.\n#### Impact\nThe cyber attack compromised the data of its customers who have used the service since July 2024, including their names, phone numbers, email addresses, and travel-related details like departure and arrival airports, hotel names, and flight numbers.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: Flickr\n#### About\nFlickr is a California-based online services provider known for its video and image hosting service. It hosts the largest collection of creative licensed photos on the web.\n#### Industry\nOnline services\n#### What happened?\nFlickr notified its users in February that their data had been compromised in a data breach caused by a cyber attack on their third-party provider.\n#### Impact\nThe data breach compromised the data of members, including their usernames, IP addresses, location data, account types, and activity on Flickr.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: San Diego Eye Bank\n#### About\nThe San Diego Eye Bank is a provider of sight restoration and preservation services founded in 1960. It collects, processes, and distributes human ocular tissues. It also engages in research and offers evaluation and therapy services.\n#### Industry\nBiotechnology Research\n#### What happened?\nThe San Diego Eye Bank became a victim of a ransomware attack that was orchestrated by the Pear ransomware group.\n#### Impact\nThe nature and quantity of data compromised in the attack are under investigation.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: Dutch Data Protection Authority\n#### About\nThe Dutch Data Protection Authority is the Netherlands ‘ independent supervisory authority for personal data processing.\n#### Industry\nPublic sector\n#### What happened?\nA security vulnerability in Ivanti Endpoint Manager Mobile was exploited by a cybercriminal to gain access to sensitive information in the Dutch Data Protection Authority and Council of Justice.\n#### Impact\nThe cyber attack compromised the personal information of employees working in the government agencies, including their names, phone numbers, and addresses.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: Iron Mountain\n#### About\nIron Mountain is a New Hampshire-based information management services provider that was founded in 1951. It operates in over 61 countries, and 95% of its clients are Fortune 1000 companies.\n#### Industry\nEnterprise Information Management\n#### What happened?\nIron Mountain became a victim of a ransomware attack that was orchestrated by the Everest ransomware gang.\n#### Impact\nThe ransomware attack has compromised the company’s internal documents and personal information belonging to its clients.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: Substack\n#### About\nSubstack is a California-based online solutions provider known for its subscription platform that offers creators an infrastructure for publishing, earning, and analytics. It is popular among journalists, media platforms, and subject matter experts.\n#### Industry\nOnline publishing\n#### What happened?\nOn 3rd February 2026, Substack discovered unauthorized access to the data of its users.\n#### Impact\nThe incident compromised users’ data, including phone numbers, email addresses, and other data.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: Conpet\n#### About\nConpet is Romania’s national oil pipeline operator with a massive pipe network of over 3800 kilometers. It offers an undisruptive supply of crude oil, liquid ethane, and gasoline to refineries across the country.\n#### Industry\nOil and gas\n#### What happened?\nConpet became a victim of a ransomware attack that was carried out by the Qilin ransomware group.\n#### Impact\nThe data breach compromised over 1 TB of the company’s information, including sensitive internal documents, personal information (like passports), and financial information.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: Hawk Law Group\n#### About\nHawk Law Group is a law firm based in the United States. It is known for its experienced lawyers who are recognized throughout the Central Savannah River Area for their civil and criminal litigation knowledge and case success.\n#### Industry\nLegal\n#### What happened?\nHawk Law Group became a victim of a ransomware attack that was orchestrated by the INC ransomware group.\n#### Impact\nThe ransomware attack has compromised the personal information of clients, including government-issued IDs, forms, and civil and criminal litigation case-related data.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: Deatak\n#### About\nDeatak is a United States-based manufacturer of flammability test instruments in the North America region, recognized for its reliable equipment and support.\n#### Industry\nManufacturing\n#### What happened?\nDeatak became a victim of a ransomware attack that was carried out by the Play ransomware group, in which the group listed the manufacturer’s name on a data breach forum.\n#### Impact\nThe ransomware attack has compromised private and confidential data, including clients’ documents, employee payroll details, IDs, and taxation and other financial information.\n```\nSource\n```\n### Victim: Eisenberg Lowrance Lundell Lofgren\n#### About\nEisenberg Lowrance Lundell Lofgren is a Utah-based law firm that offers contingency fee lawyers who specialize in personal injury, immigration, and criminal defense.\n#### Industry\nLegal\n#### What happened?\nEisenberg Lowrance Lundell Lofgren became a target of a ransomware attack orchestrated by the INC ransomware group.\n#### Impact\nThe ransomware attack has compromised the personal information of clients, including their government-issued IDs and case-related information.\n```\nSource\n```\n### To be continued\nWe have already seen some of the most devastating data breaches In February 2026. Keep checking this space as we update our list of February’s Top data breaches just as we did in January 2026, with a closer look at the top data breaches, how they happened, and their impact.\nNote: Our list only highlights the breaches that have either occurred in 2026 or reported/disclosed in 2026. All breaches reported in previous years, as of 2026, will be excluded from the list.",

    "content": "# February 2026 Patch Tuesday: Key Updates on Security Vulnerabilities\nFebruary 2026 Patch Tuesday marks a significant moment for Windows users and IT administrators alike, as Microsoft takes proactive measures to address pressing security concerns. This month’s updates include over 50 Microsoft security patches February 2026 aimed at eliminating vulnerabilities, notably six critical zero-day vulnerabilities currently being exploited by cybercriminals. Among these CVE vulnerabilities February 2026, CVE-2026-21510, which targets Windows Shell, exemplifies the type of urgent threat that prompt users to prioritize their system security. With the rise of cyber threats, ensuring timely Windows updates February 2026 is essential for maintaining a secure operating environment. Stay informed on the Patch Tuesday highlights February 2026 to safeguard your data from potential breaches and exploits that could arise from unpatched systems.\nIn the realm of cybersecurity, the February 2026 Patch Tuesday signifies an important release of software updates aimed at bolstering system defenses. Following Microsoft’s tradition, this event comes with an extensive package of critical updates designed to mitigate the risks posed by various vulnerabilities. February 2026’s noteworthy features include a mix of security improvements that address potential loopholes, including responses to urgent CVE vulnerabilities aimed at enhancing overall network protection. With the escalation of cyber threats, organizations must prioritize these updates to remain resilient against attacks, especially those exploiting zero-day vulnerabilities. By staying abreast of these patches, users can shield their systems from emerging threats and ensure their data remains secure.\n## Overview of Microsoft Security Patches Released in February 2026\nOn February 10, 2026, Microsoft rolled out a significant number of security updates aimed at addressing over 50 vulnerabilities across its various Windows operating systems and software applications. Among the updates, the most striking were the six critical zero-day vulnerabilities that were actively being exploited, indicating a pressing need for users to install these patches promptly to safeguard their systems. Zero-day vulnerabilities represent security holes that hackers can exploit before the vendor even releases a fix, which emphasizes the importance of these updates for both personal and enterprise environments.\nEach of these updates not only addresses the immediate threat posed by the zero-day vulnerabilities but also reinforces the overall security framework of Windows systems. The patches included fixes for known CVE vulnerabilities, like CVE-2026-21510 and CVE-2026-21513, which could allow attackers to bypass critical security measures. As organizations face an ever-evolving landscape of threats, the timely application of Microsoft’s security patches is vital for maintaining system integrity and protecting sensitive data.\n## Details on Zero-Day Vulnerabilities Addressed\nFebruary 2026’s Patch Tuesday was particularly notable for its focus on zero-day vulnerabilities, which are critical exploits that can compromise system security until they are patched. For example, CVE-2026-21510 targets Windows Shell, allowing attackers a method to execute arbitrary code through deceptive links. Such vulnerabilities highlight the necessity for users to remain vigilant and ensure their systems are updated regularly to mitigate the risk of exploitation.\nAnother noteworthy vulnerability is CVE-2026-21533, which can allow local users to elevate their privileges significantly within Windows Remote Desktop Services. Privilege escalation risks are especially concerning for users with administrative access, as they can lead to serious breaches of system control. Patching these vulnerabilities is crucial not only to protect individual users but also to strengthen the defenses of entire corporate networks.\n## Patch Tuesday Highlights for February 2026: Essential Updates\nThe Patch Tuesday highlights for February 2026 included critical updates aimed at resolving serious vulnerabilities across various platforms and applications. In addition to the zero-day exploits, Microsoft addressed multiple remote code execution vulnerabilities that could potentially allow attackers to take control of affected systems. Such updates reinforce the need for users and IT departments to stay informed about the latest patches and to implement them without delay.\nOne major highlight this month was the focus on integrated development environments (IDEs) such as GitHub Copilot, which required urgent patches due to vulnerabilities like CVE-2026-21516. Developers are particularly susceptible to targeted attacks, given their access to sensitive coding environments and API keys. Thus, it is recommended that organizations fortify their developer environments with the most recent security patches released during the February 2026 Patch Tuesday.\n## Understanding the Implications of CVE Vulnerabilities\nCVE vulnerabilities play a crucial role in cybersecurity by providing a standardized method to identify and address known security flaws. The vulnerabilities patched in February 2026, including CVE-2026-21510 and CVE-2026-21513, serve as stark reminders of how easily systems can be compromised if they remain unpatched. Regularly updating software is essential for mitigating risk, as these known vulnerabilities become prime targets for malicious actors.\nMonitoring CVE databases and staying informed about Microsoft security patches in February 2026 not only assists in immediate remediation but also contributes to long-term cybersecurity hygiene. Users and administrators should adopt a proactive stance when it comes to patch management to ensure they are not leaving their systems vulnerable to known exploits.\n## AI Vulnerabilities and Their Consequences in February 2026\nThis month’s Patch Tuesday also underscored the critical vulnerabilities associated with AI technologies, particularly those that can be manipulated through prompt injections. Flaws identified within AI platforms, such as those impacting GitHub Copilot, point to a growing trend where AI systems, if not secured effectively, could serve as conduits for executing harmful commands or accessing sensitive information.\nAs organizations increasingly integrate AI into their workflows, acknowledging these risks becomes paramount. Applying the updates provided in the February 2026 Microsoft security patches is an essential step toward safeguarding against these potential threats. Developers must adopt a security-first mindset, ensuring that the systems they design mitigate risks associated with AI usage.\n## Best Practices for Applying Security Patches from Microsoft in February 2026\nWhen it comes to applying the February 2026 security patches from Microsoft, following best practices is crucial for both individual and organizational security. First and foremost, users should conduct regular backups of their data before initiating any updates. This precaution can save important files and configurations in case something goes wrong during the patching process.\nAdditionally, organizations should establish a well-defined patch management strategy. This includes testing patches in a controlled environment before broad deployment, monitoring user feedback regarding potential issues, and maintaining documentation of all changes made. Information sources like askwoody.com can provide insights on known issues related to the updates, helping to streamline the patching process and minimize any disruptions.\n## The Importance of Staying Updated with Microsoft’s Security Guidance\nRegularly consulting Microsoft’s security advisories is key to staying ahead of potential threats. The February 2026 Patch Tuesday not only provided a wealth of updates but also highlighted the serious implications of failing to secure systems against identified vulnerabilities. Organizations that actively monitor and respond to these advisories are better equipped to protect their digital infrastructure from evolving cyber threats.\nBy cultivating a security-aware culture that encourages timely application of updates and ongoing staff training, businesses can significantly enhance their resilience against cyber threats. Understanding the latest vulnerabilities and how they can affect business operations also allows IT teams to prioritize resources effectively and implement the most essential security measures.\n## Conclusion: Preparing for Future Cyber Threats Beyond February 2026\nAs we move beyond February 2026, it is imperative to remain vigilant in the face of ever-evolving cyber threats. The patch updates issued by Microsoft reflect a proactive approach to addressing vulnerabilities but underscore that security is an ongoing process that requires consistent attention. Ensuring that all systems are regularly updated can safeguard against future zero-day vulnerabilities and newly discovered CVEs.\nMoreover, organizations should foster a security mindset among employees, educating them about the importance of cybersecurity practices, including recognizing phishing attempts and proper data handling techniques. As technology continues to advance, so do the tactics of cybercriminals, making it essential for everyone to understand their role in maintaining a secure digital environment.\n## Frequently Asked Questions\n### What vulnerabilities were addressed in the February 2026 Patch Tuesday updates?\nThe February 2026 Patch Tuesday updates addressed more than 50 security vulnerabilities, including six critical zero-day vulnerabilities, notably CVE-2026-21510, which allows attackers to bypass Windows security features and execute malicious content.\n### How does the CVE-2026-21510 vulnerability impact Windows systems during February 2026 Patch Tuesday?\nCVE-2026-21510 is a significant security feature bypass vulnerability in Windows Shell, affecting all supported Windows versions. A simple click on a malicious link can enable attackers to execute code without user consent.\n### What are zero-day vulnerabilities in the February 2026 Patch Tuesday context?\nZero-day vulnerabilities are security flaws that are exploited by attackers before the vendor releases a patch. This month’s updates are particularly noteworthy due to the presence of several critical zero-day exploits that threaten user safety. IT professionals and with interest in system maintenance should pay close attention to the details surrounding Microsoft’s security patches for February 2026, as these updates will significantly contribute to closing gaps that cyber attackers may exploit. By staying informed about these updates, users can better protect their systems against potential threats."
      },

        "type": "text",
        "text": "Microsoft’s February 2026 Patch Tuesday has been a significant event for IT security managers and system administrators alike, as the company rolled out updates addressing over 50 vulnerabilities across its software suite. Among these, six critical zero-day vulnerabilities have emerged, each with the potential for exploitation in real-world scenarios. Notably, vulnerabilities like CVE-2026-21510 demonstrate how easily attackers can bypass security measures simply through user interaction, emphasizing the need for vigilance from end-users as well as comprehensive patch management from administrators."
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "CVE-2026-21510, a bypass vulnerability discovered in Windows Shell, highlights a worrying trend where unsolicited clicks can lead to unauthorized execution of commands. This reinforcement of user awareness about clicking on suspicious links is essential, even as patches are deployed. Furthermore, the additional zero-days concerning Microsoft Office and browser components, namely CVE-2026-21513 and CVE-2026-21514, point towards the ongoing evolution of threats that specifically target widely used applications, underscoring the significance of timely updates and security awareness training."
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "Additionally, the varying impact levels of the vulnerabilities patched this month, which include privilege escalation and denial-of-service threats in critical components like Windows Remote Desktop Services, demonstrate the layered nature of potential risks. As mentioned by experts like Chris Goettl and Kev Breen, the implications of not applying these updates swiftly can be severe, especially for organizations relying on remote work infrastructures. The introduction of fixes for remote code execution vulnerabilities within development environments also signals a growing intersection between software development processes and cybersecurity, necessitating a proactive approach involving both developers and security teams."
      },

The risks posed by such vulnerabilities reflect a need to thoroughly vet AI systems while implementing best practices for access controls. The call for applying least-privilege principles is particularly relevant as organizations navigate the delicate balance between leveraging cutting-edge technologies and safeguarding sensitive data against emerging threats."

    "content": "# 5 cybersecurity trends to watch in 2026 | Cybersecurity Dive\nAn article from\n![site logo](https://d12v9rtnomnebu.cloudfront.net/logo/printer_friendly/cybersecuritydive.jpg)\nDeep Dive\n# 5 cybersecurity trends to watch in 2026\nCorporations across the globe are facing a dynamic risk environment, as AI adoption surges with few guardrails, business resilience takes center stage and the insurance industry raises major concerns.\nPublished Jan. 23, 2026\n[![David Jones's headshot](https://d1b6lhn2ymmy1x.cloudfront.net/journalist-headshots/cybersecurity/jones-david-circle-150x150.png)](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/editors/djones/)\n[David Jones](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/editors/djones/)\nReporter\n* [![Share this article](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/static/img/social_icons/share-icon.svg?472316191225)\n  Share](javascript:void(0))\n  + [![Copy link](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/static/img/social_icons/share_dropdown/share-link-box.svg?472316191225)\n    Copy link](javascript:void(0))\n  + [![Email this page](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/static/img/social_icons/share_dropdown/email.svg?472316191225)\n    Email](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#a09ff3d5c2cac5c3d49d95859290c3d9c2c5d2d3c5c3d5d2c9d4d9859290d4d2c5cec4d3859290d4cf859290d7c1d4c3c8859290c9ce8592909290929686c1cdd09be2cfc4d99dc8d4d4d0d38593e18f8fd7d7d78ec3d9c2c5d2d3c5c3d5d2c9d4d9c4c9d6c58ec3cfcd8fcec5d7d38f958dc3d9c2c5d2d3c5c3d5d2c9d4d98dd4d2c5cec4d38d929092968f9891909395948f)\n  + [![Post to LinkedIn](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/static/img/social_icons/share_dropdown/linkedin.svg?472316191225)\n    LinkedIn](https://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&url=https%3A//www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/5-cybersecurity-trends-2026/810354/&title=5%20cybersecurity%20trends%20to%20watch%20in%202026)\n  + [![Post on X](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/static/img/social_icons/share_dropdown/x.svg?472316191225)\n    X/Twitter](https://twitter.com/intent/tweet?text=5%20cybersecurity%20trends%20to%20watch%20in%202026%20https%3A//www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/5-cybersecurity-trends-2026/810354/%20via%20@CyberSecDive)\n  + [![Share on Facebook](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/static/img/social_icons/share_dropdown/facebook.svg?472316191225)\n    Facebook](https://www.facebook.com/sharer/sharer.php?u=https%3A//www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/5-cybersecurity-trends-2026/810354/)\n  + [![Print this page](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/static/img/social_icons/share_dropdown/print.svg?472316191225)\n    Print](javascript:window.print())\n* [![License this article](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/static/img/social_icons/article_page/license-icon.svg?472316191225)\n  License](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/selfservice/article-licensing/submit/?newspostUrl=https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/5-cybersecurity-trends-2026/810354/)\n* [![Set preferred source](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/static/img/social_icons/article_page/bookmark-add.svg?472316191225)\n  Add us on Google](https://www.google.com/preferences/source?q=https://www.cybersecuritydive.com)\n![Rendered image depicting global networks.](https://imgproxy.divecdn.com/hHzci3MZFoHm2LdTYYxyAjNcId-LsFyi0wtsHCsseZQ/g:ce/rs:fill:1200:675:1/Z3M6Ly9kaXZlc2l0ZS1zdG9yYWdlL2RpdmVpbWFnZS9HZXR0eUltYWdlcy0xMjEzMjIzOTU2LmpwZw==.webp)\nGetty Images\nThe cybersecurity sector faced historic pressure in 2025. New AI tools changed the way we work, but at the same time posed new forms of cyber risk to organizations who adopt them.\nMeanwhile, cybercrime groups employed an evolving menu of techniques to disrupt key industries, forcing businesses and government authorities to shift their emphasis toward operational resilience and managing the long-term financial impact of cyber incidents.  \nHere are five key trends that will shape cyber in 2026:\n**1. AI governance and guardrails now front and center**\nThe adoption of artificial intelligence moved faster over the past year than most anyone could have anticipated. \nAn international arms race has commenced between major economic powers, led by the U.S. and China, over who will lead AI transformation. At the same time, companies are rushing to incorporate AI into their profit models, betting both on major gains in productivity as well as the technology supercharging their core product lines. \nBut this rapid embrace of AI brings growing concerns over whether companies have created the proper guardrails and governance structures to ensure their AI programs are secure and cannot be used by malicious actors to exfiltrate corporate data, exploit customers or compromise supply chains. \n“There is a gap between how fast organizations are adopting AI and the maturity of their governance framework,” Morgan Adamski, cyber, data and tech risk deputy leader at PwC told Cybersecurity Dive. “Many are experimenting with agentic and generative AI to drive productivity or efficiency, but often, there are no guardrails in place from a security perspective.”\nAI has moved quickly to become one of the top business cyber risks among global companies. A January report from Allianz Commercial shows AI risk jumped from number 10 to the [second-leading business risk concern over the past year](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/ai-surges-business-risk-cybersecurity-holds/809620/), based on a survey of more than 3,300 risk management professionals. \nLook for AI risk to drive organizations in 2026 to focus more on establishing [proper parameters and security for their AI programs](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/ai-augment-security-identity-soc/803608/).\n**2. Cybersecurity regulatory shifts shape disclosures**\nThe regulatory environment for cyber has undergone significant changes in the past year. The Trump administration shifted toward a more nuanced approach, both in terms of oversight and implementation of cyber risk compared with how the Biden administration regulated it. That means oversight in the information security space is not going away but instead will allow markets forces more room to operate.\n“Rather than uniformly pulling back or pursuing broad regulatory expansion, the government is continuing to assess where clearer expectations, coordination, or enforcement are warranted in response to a dynamic threat landscape,” said Haiman Wong, resident fellow, cybersecurity and emerging threats at the R Street Institute. \nThis is particularly the case for critical infrastructure, which is largely owned by the private sector and already faces heightened cyber risk.\nA November 2025 decision by the Securities and Exchange Commission to [drop a landmark civil fraud case against SolarWinds](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/sec-drops-civil-fraud-case-solarwinds/806126/) was widely considered a welcome development for the business community. The 2023 suit alleged that SolarWinds failed to disclose known cyber risks to investors during the years leading up to the 2020 Sunburst cyberattacks. \nA federal judge had previously dismissed most of the allegations on the grounds the SEC misapplied a Depression-era law to the company’s alleged failure to implement security controls. That legal resolution was also seen as a win for the CISO community, as SolarWinds’ CISO Tim Brown had also faced enforcement action by the SEC in the regulatory agency’s case. \nSagar Ravi, a partner at McDermott Will & Schulte and a former chief of the Complex Frauds & Cyberscrime Unit at the U.S. Attorney’s Office for the Southern District of New York, said the decision to drop the SolarWinds case hopefully signals a move to recognize companies should not be punished for falling victim to sophisticated cyber threat actors. It also emphasizes the need for cyber risk transparency, he said.\n“I think the focus is going to be on [enforcing] cybersecurity disclosure rules” in material incident reports on form 8-K or additional disclosures of strategy in annual reports, Ravi told Cybersecurity Dive. \nRavi hopes the SEC instead emphasizes ensuring proper post-breach disclosure rather than conducting investigations that review pre-incident decision making. \n**3. Cyber insurance enters new phase in pricing, coverage**\nThe insurance market has seen its share of turbulence as it struggled to address cyber risk. For years, companies struggled to obtain cybersecurity coverage amid the increased threat of ransomware and fears about the rise of state-linked hackers.\nMost recently, global insurers have expanded their commitment to cyber risk, and recent legal cases involving [war exclusions language](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/merck-settlement-notpetya-insurance/703922/) related to the NotPetya attacks has provided greater clarity on coverage. Even so, the insurance industry has begun questioning its dependence on the U.S. market, and whether current premium levels for cyber insurance can remain over the long haul. \nThat could mean diversification of the cyber insurance market. Large corporations in the U.S. represent a significant percentage of U.S. policy holders in the cyber market, so insurance companies need to [expand into new markets](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/cyber-insurance-reduce-losses-diversification/761128/) such as small- to midsized businesses**,** risk analytics firmCyberCube said in a September report. Specialist insurer Beazley late last year said it remains committed to the U.S. market, but [warned of a weak pricing environment](https://beazley2023tf.q4web.com/news/news-details/2025/Trading-Statement-c8cf23f90/default.aspx) for cybersecurity coverage. \nIn order to maintain favorable coverage, insurers are now heavily scrutinizing enterprise security practices, according to risk experts. \n“Not too long ago, you could get cyber insurance with basic antivirus and a firewall,” Monica Shokrai, head of business risk and insurance at Google Cloud said. “Today, if you don’t have phishing-resistant MFA, XDR and immutable backups, you won’t just pay more. You may not get access to coverage.”\n**4. CVE crisis resolved while patching challenges remain**\nOne of the most pressing challenges for security teams in recent years has been how to identify, prioritize and remediate critical flaws discovered in widely used software.\nThese security vulnerabilities are often the gateway used by hackers to launch malicious cyberattacks by abusing the very security tools and software that critical industries and government agencies rely on to manage and protect their [IT networks and maintain operational resilience](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/network-security-defects-erode-defense/738387/).\nThe security sector was thrown into crisis in April of last year when U.S. government funding nearly collapsed for the Common Exposures and Vulnerabilities (CVE) program. An agreement was eventually reached between CISA and the Mitre Corp. to maintain support for 11 months, and CISA officials in September [pledged to back future funding](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/cisa-pledges-robust-support-for-funding-further-development-of-cve-program/760020/), releasing a road map that outlines additional support measures. \n“CISA is asserting our leadership role to modernize the CVE Program, broaden adoption of known exploited vulnerabilities and reduce the prevalence of vulnerabilities by driving adoption of Secure by Design principles,” Nick Andersen, executive assistant director for cybersecurity at CISA told Cybersecurity Dive earlier this month. “In collaboration with the global cybersecurity community, CISA is working to deliver a well-governed, trusted, and responsive CVE Program aimed to enhance the quality of vulnerability data and global cybersecurity resilience.”\nSoftware security experts say the CVE funding crisis is a wake-up call for the industry to develop proactive measures to finally address insecure software.\n“Organizations need multisource, context-aware intelligence layered on top of CVE so each record reflects what actually matters: Exploitability, reach, prevalence in real dependency graphs, and whether there’s a safe upgrade path,” Brian Fox, co-founder and CTO at Sonatype told Cybersecurity Dive.\n**5. Operational resilience becomes the new watchword for cyberattack readiness**\nDuring much of 2025, companies around the globe were forced to confront a significant shift in cyber resilience. Cyber threat groups were no longer focused just on the exfiltration of data as their main objective, but instead on causing massive disruption to business operations. \nA social engineering attack on [UK department store Marks & Spencer](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/marks-spencer-restores-some-online-order-operations-following-cyberattack/750305/), the hack of United Natural Foods and a crippling hack of [automaker Jaguar Land Rover](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/news/auto-sector-cyber-threats-business-continuity/802974/) served as graphic examples in 2025 of how easily a successful cyberattack can disrupt production capacity, as well as major supply chains. \nSecurity researchers said those cyberattacks were part of a deliberate strategy by threat actors to impose maximum pressure on major industries for monetary gain.\n“Over the past year, we witnessed a fundamental shift in the attacker playbook, where financially motivated groups like Muddled Libra (Scattered Spider) moved beyond simple data theft to deliberate operational sabotage,” said Sam Rubin, senior vice president, Unit 42 at Palo Alto Networks. “By exploiting the human element through sophisticated ‘vishing’ and manipulating help desks, these actors proved they could paralyze entire enterprise networks and stop businesses in their tracks to maximize extortion leverage.”\nCorporate boards and C-suite executives are under pressure to ensure cyber risk is a key factor in their overall business resilience strategy, experts said security leaders will be tasked with developing specific plans on how to maintain operations and protect supply chains in the face of a catastrophic IT or security event.\n* [![Set preferred source](https://www.cybersecuritydive.com/static/img/social_icons/article_page/bookmark-add.svg?472316191225)\n  Add us on Large corporations in the U.S. represent a significant percentage of U.S. policy holders in the cyber market, so insurance companies need to expand into new markets such as small- to midsized businesses , risk analytics firm CyberCube said in a September report. Specialist insurer Beazley late last year said it remains committed to the U.S. market, but warned of a weak pricing environment for cybersecurity coverage."
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "In order to maintain favorable coverage, insurers are now heavily scrutinizing enterprise security practices, according to risk experts."
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "“Not too long ago, you could get cyber insurance with basic antivirus and a firewall,” Monica Shokrai, head of business risk and insurance at Google Cloud said. “Today, if you don’t have phishing-resistant MFA, XDR and immutable backups, you won’t just pay more. You may not get access to coverage.”"
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "4. CVE crisis resolved while patching challenges remain"
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "One of the most pressing challenges for security teams in recent years has been how to identify, prioritize and remediate critical flaws discovered in widely used software."
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "These security vulnerabilities are often the gateway used by hackers to launch malicious cyberattacks by abusing the very security tools and software that critical industries and government agencies rely on to manage and protect their IT networks and maintain operational resilience ."
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "The security sector was thrown into crisis in April of last year when U.S. government funding nearly collapsed for the Common Exposures and Vulnerabilities (CVE) program. An agreement was eventually reached between CISA and the Mitre Corp. to maintain support for 11 months, and CISA officials in September pledged to back future funding , releasing a road map that outlines additional support measures."
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "“CISA is asserting our leadership role to modernize the CVE Program, broaden adoption of known exploited vulnerabilities and reduce the prevalence of vulnerabilities by driving adoption of Secure by Design principles,” Nick Andersen, executive assistant director for cybersecurity at CISA told Cybersecurity Dive earlier this month. “In collaboration with the global cybersecurity community, CISA is working to deliver a well-governed, trusted, and responsive CVE Program aimed to enhance the quality of vulnerability data and global cybersecurity resilience.”"
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "Software security experts say the CVE funding crisis is a wake-up call for the industry to develop proactive measures to finally address insecure software."
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "“Organizations need multisource, context-aware intelligence layered on top of CVE so each record reflects what actually matters: Exploitability, reach, prevalence in real dependency graphs, and whether there’s a safe upgrade path,” Brian Fox, co-founder and CTO at Sonatype told Cybersecurity Dive."
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "5. Operational resilience becomes the new watchword for cyberattack readiness"
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "During much of 2025, companies around the globe were forced to confront a significant shift in cyber resilience. Cyber threat groups were no longer focused just on the exfiltration of data as their main objective, but instead on causing massive disruption to business operations."
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "A social engineering attack on UK department store Marks & Spencer , the hack of United Natural Foods and a crippling hack of automaker Jaguar Land Rover served as graphic examples in 2025 of how easily a successful cyberattack can disrupt production capacity, as well as major supply chains."
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "Security researchers said those cyberattacks were part of a deliberate strategy by threat actors to impose maximum pressure on major industries for monetary gain."
      },
      {
        "type": "text",
        "text": "“ Over the past year, we witnessed a fundamental shift in the attacker playbook, where financially motivated groups like Muddled Libra (Scattered Spider) moved beyond simple data theft to deliberate operational sabotage,” said Sam Rubin, senior vice president, Unit 42 at Palo Alto Networks. “By exploiting the human element through sophisticated ‘vishing’ and manipulating help desks, these actors proved they could paralyze entire enterprise networks and stop businesses in their tracks to maximize extortion leverage.”"
      },

Including 6 Zero-days\nBy\n[Guru Baran](https://cybersecuritynews.com/author/guru/)\nFebruary 10, 2026\n[![Microsoft Patch Tuesday February 2026](https://i2.wp.com/blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgh7zWuvOHZ2dY4vNIIAOqLOjQ721C2jhApzjJWAVSSL9sqnj9cVbSsY5IfNfGnpjTEOXTzrjIWFAefNcCnHOsBTbD7oNO6Y-yezwDA7ssWKOK3MurJfafibJsmYrWePIvS7Raatx0JjjEk12AQH_kyt_SxWGVwL1XfCT8NypbpeBvL-DPAmSdK8t7tq7tR/s16000/Microsoft%20Patch%20Tuesday%20Feburary%202026.webp?w=1068&resize=1068,0&ssl=1 Patch Tuesday February 2026\nMicrosoft released its February 2026 Patch Tuesday updates on February 10, addressing 54 vulnerabilities, including six zero-days across Windows, Office, Azure, and developer tools.\nThe updates fix issues in products like [Windows Remote Desktop Services](https://cybersecuritynews.com/windows-remote-desktop-services-rce-vulnerability/), Microsoft Defender, Azure services, GitHub Copilot, Visual Studio Code, Microsoft Exchange, and Office apps.\nSeverity ratings include two Critical flaws and numerous Important ones, with types including remote code execution (RCE), elevation of privilege (EoP), information disclosure, spoofing, denial-of-service (DoS), and security feature bypass. Microsoft assigns customer action as required for all listed CVEs and urges immediate patching.\n| Vulnerability Type | Count |\n| --- | --- |\n| Remote Code Execution | 11​ |\n| Denial of Service | 3​ |\n| Elevation of Privilege | 23​ |\n| Information Disclosure | 5​ |\n| Security Feature Bypass | 5​ |\n| Spoofing | 7​ |\n| **Total** | **54**​ |\n## **Zero-Day Vulnerabilities**\nSix zero-days were patched, marked as publicly disclosed and/or exploited prior to release. These include:\n* [CVE-2026-21514](https://cybersecuritynews.com/microsoft-office-word-0-day-vulnerability/): Security feature bypass in Microsoft Office Word.\n* [CVE-2026-21513](https://cybersecuritynews.com/mshtml-framework-0-day-vulnerability/): Security feature bypass in MSHTML Framework.\n* [CVE-2026-21510](https://cybersecuritynews.com/windows-shell-security-feature-0-day/): Security feature bypass in Windows Shell.\n* [CVE-2026-21533](https://cybersecuritynews.com/windows-remote-desktop-services-0-day-vulnerability/): EoP in Windows Remote Desktop Services.\n* [CVE-2026-21525](https://cybersecuritynews.com/windows-rrasman-0-day-vulnerability/): DoS in Windows Remote Access Connection Manager.\n* [CVE-2026-21519](https://cybersecuritynews.com/desktop-window-manager-0-day/): EoP in Desktop Window Manager.\nAttackers could chain these for broader compromise, such as bypassing protections to execute code or escalate privileges.\n## **Critical Vulnerabilities**\nTwo Critical vulnerabilities demand priority:\n[![google](https://thecybernews.com/csngoogle.svg)](https://www.google.com/preferences/source?q=cybersecuritynews.com)\n| CVE ID | Type | Affected Product | CVSS Implication |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| CVE-2026-23655 | Information Disclosure | Azure Compute Gallery (ACI Confidential Containers) | Allows sensitive data leak from confidential workloads. |\n| CVE-2026-21522 | Elevation of Privilege | Azure Compute Gallery (ACI Confidential Containers) | Enables privilege escalation in container environments. |\nThese Azure flaws highlight risks in cloud-native confidential computing.\nRCE flaws pose high risks in cloud and endpoint tools:\n* CVE-2026-21537: RCE in Microsoft Defender for Endpoint Linux Extension.\n* CVE-2026-21531: RCE in Azure SDK for Python.\n* CVE-2026-21523: RCE in GitHub Copilot and Visual Studio Code.\n* CVE-2026-21516: RCE in GitHub Copilot for JetBrains.\n* CVE-2026-21256: RCE in GitHub Copilot and Visual Studio.\nOffice issues include spoofing in Outlook (CVE-2026-21527, CVE-2026-21260), info disclosure/EoP in Excel (CVE-2026-21261, CVE-2026-21259, CVE-2026-21258), and Word bypass (CVE-2026-21514). Windows sees EoP in HTTP.sys (CVE-2026-21250), Hyper-V bypass (CVE-2026-21255), and storage (CVE-2026-21508).\nAzure-specific: Spoofing in HDInsight (CVE-2026-21529), info disclosure in IoT Explorer SDK (CVE-2026-21528). Other: XSS spoofing in Azure DevOps (CVE-2026-21512).\nElevated risks target developers (Copilot/VS Code), enterprises (Azure/Exchange), and endpoints (Windows/Defender). Exploitation could lead to data theft, lateral movement, or full compromise.\nThe table below summarizes the CVEs found in the provided text, including links to the official Microsoft Security Response Center (MSRC) pages for each vulnerability, along with their impact, severity, and affected product details.\n### **Microsoft Security Updates – February 10, 2026**\n| **CVE ID** | **Impact** When you look a little more closely, you start to realize that there is a lot going on here. February can be a bit of a cold, dull month, but Microsoft has decided to heat things up a bit. The good news, there’s not a lot of CVEs to deal with, the bad news, there’s actually a lot to unpack here.     "title": "6 Actively Exploited Zero-Days Patched by Microsoft With February 2026 Updates - SecurityWeek",

UPDATE: CISA has added the six zero-days to its KEV catalog. Adam Meyers, Head of Counter Adversary Operations at CrowdStrike, told SecurityWeek, “The CVE-2026-21533 exploit binary modifies a service configuration key, replacing it with an attacker-controlled key, which could enable adversaries to escalate privileges to add a new user to the Administrator group.",

    "content": "# 6 Actively Exploited Zero-Days Patched by Microsoft With February 2026 Updates - SecurityWeek\n![Windows security](https://www.securityweek.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/10/Windows-Kernel-BSOD.jpg)\n**Microsoft’s February 2026 Patch Tuesday updates fix roughly 60 vulnerabilities found in the company’s products, including six actively exploited zero-days.**\nThe zero-days are:\n* [CVE-2026-21510](https://msrc.microsoft.com/update-guide/vulnerability/CVE-2026-21510): a Windows SmartScreen and Windows Shell security prompts bypass that can be exploited by convincing the targeted user to open a malicious link or shortcut file.\n* [CVE-2026-21514](https://msrc.microsoft.com/update-guide/vulnerability/CVE-2026-21514): a vulnerability that allows an attacker to bypass OLE mitigations in Microsoft 365 and Office by tricking the target into opening a malicious Office file.\n* [CVE-2026-21513](https://msrc.microsoft.com/update-guide/vulnerability/CVE-2026-21513): an Internet Explorer issue that allows an attacker to bypass security controls and potentially execute code by convincing the victim to open a malicious HTML or LNK file.\n* [CVE-2026-21519](https://msrc.microsoft.com/update-guide/vulnerability/CVE-2026-21519): a Windows Desktop Window Manager flaw that can be exploited by a local attacker for privilege escalation.\n* [CVE-2026-21533](https://msrc.microsoft.com/update-guide/vulnerability/CVE-2026-21533): a Windows Remote Desktop Services vulnerability that allows an attacker to escalate privileges to System.\n* [CVE-2026-21525](https://msrc.microsoft.com/update-guide/vulnerability/CVE-2026-21525): a Windows Remote Access Connection Manager bug that can be exploited for local DoS attacks.\nThere appears to be no public information about attacks exploiting these zero-days.\nHowever, it’s worth noting that for the discovery of both CVE-2026-21510 and CVE-2026-21514 Microsoft credited Google Threat Intelligence Group (GTIG), its own security teams, and an anonymous researcher. CVE-2026-21513 was discovered by Microsoft and GTIG.\nThis suggests that some of these vulnerabilities may have been exploited by the same threat actors or in the same attacks. Google has been tracking attacks conducted by [commercial spyware vendors](https://www.securityweek.com/google-links-over-60-zero-days-to-commercial-spyware-vendors/), [state-sponsored APTs, and profit-driven cybercriminals](https://www.securityweek.com/apts-cybercriminals-widely-exploiting-winrar-vulnerability), but nation-state hackers are often behind campaigns involving these types of zero-days.\nCVE-2026-21510, CVE-2026-21514 and CVE-2026-21513 are all flagged as ‘publicly disclosed’ in [Microsoft’s advisories](https://msrc.microsoft.com/update-guide/releaseNote/2026-Feb).\nCVE-2026-21519 was discovered by Microsoft’s own researchers. The tech giant has credited the cybersecurity firm CrowdStrike with the discovery of CVE-2026-21533 and Acros Security with CVE-2026-21525.\n*SecurityWeek* has reached out to both Acros and CrowdStrike for information on the attacks exploiting the zero-days and will update this article if they respond.\nIn addition to Windows and Office, Microsoft has patched vulnerabilities in Azure, Windows Defender, Exchange Server, .NET, GitHub Copilot, Edge, and Power BI.\n**UPDATE:** CISA has [added the six zero-days](https://www.cisa.gov/news-events/alerts/2026/02/10/cisa-adds-six-known-exploited-vulnerabilities-catalog) to its KEV catalog.\nAdam Meyers, Head of Counter Adversary Operations at CrowdStrike, told *SecurityWeek*, “The CVE-2026-21533 exploit binary modifies a service configuration key, replacing it with an attacker-controlled key, which could enable adversaries to escalate privileges to add a new user to the Administrator group. While CrowdStrike does not currently attribute this activity to a specific target or adversary, threat actors possessing the exploit binaries will likely accelerate their attempts to use or sell CVE-2026-21533 in the near term.”\nMitja Kolsek, CEO of Acros Security, told *SecurityWeek*, “We found an exploit for this issue in December 2025 in a public malware repository while searching for an exploit for CVE-2025-59230. This issue turned out to be a 0day at the time, so we [patched it](http://blog.0patch.com/2025/12/free-micropatches-for-windows-remote.html) and reported it to Microsoft. We don’t have any information on it having been exploited, but the quality of the combined exploit for both issues suggested professional work.”\n**Related**: [Patch Tuesday: Adobe Fixes 44 Vulnerabilities in Creative Apps](https://www.securityweek.com/patch-tuesday-adobe-fixes-44-vulnerabilities-in-creative-apps/)\n**Related**: [Russia’s APT28 Rapidly Weaponizes Newly Patched Office Vulnerability](https://www.securityweek.com/russias-apt28-rapidly-weaponizes-newly-patched-office-vulnerability/)\n**Related**: [SmarterTools Hit by Ransomware via Vulnerability in Its Own Product](https://www.securityweek.com/smartertools-hit-by-ransomware-via-vulnerability-in-its-own-product/)\n![](https://www.securityweek.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/Ed-Kovacs.jpg)\nWritten By\n[Eduard Kovacs](https://www.securityweek.com/contributors/eduard-kovacs/ \"Posts by Eduard Kovacs\")\nEduard Kovacs (@EduardKovacs) is the managing editor at SecurityWeek. He worked as a high school IT teacher before starting a career in journalism in 2011. Eduard holds a bachelor’s degree in industrial informatics and a master’s degree in computer techniques applied in electrical engineering.\n## More from [Eduard Kovacs](https://www.securityweek.com/contributors/eduard-kovacs/ \"Posts by Eduard Kovacs\")\n* [Hacktivists, State Actors, Cybercriminals Target Global Defense Industry, Google # Top 3 Cybersecurity News Stories in February 2026

## 1. Microsoft Patch Tuesday: 54 Vulnerabilities Fixed Including 6 Actively Exploited Zero-Days [[S:2,4,5]]

On **February 10, 2026**, Microsoft released its Patch Tuesday updates addressing **54 vulnerabilities** across Windows, Office, Azure, and developer tools. The most critical aspect of this update was the patching of **six zero-day vulnerabilities** that were actively being exploited in the wild [[S:4,5]].

### The Six Zero-Days:
- **CVE-2026-21510**: Windows Shell security feature bypass allowing attackers to execute code via malicious links [[S:5]]
- **CVE-2026-21514**: Microsoft Office Word security bypass enabling OLE mitigation bypass [[S:4,5]]
- **CVE-2026-21513**: MSHTML Framework (Internet Explorer) security bypass [[S:4,5]]
- **CVE-2026-21519**: Desktop Window Manager elevation of privilege vulnerability [[S:4,5]]
- **CVE-2026-21533**: Windows Remote Desktop Services privilege escalation to SYSTEM level [[S:4,5]]
- **CVE-2026-21525**: Windows Remote Access Connection Manager denial-of-service [[S:4,5]]

### Key Details:
- Google Threat Intelligence Group (GTIG) was credited with discovering several of these vulnerabilities, suggesting possible nation-state or commercial spyware vendor involvement [[S:5]]
- CrowdStrike discovered CVE-2026-21533, noting that the exploit modifies service configuration keys to enable privilege escalation [[S:5]]
- Two **Critical** severity vulnerabilities were also patched in Azure Compute Gallery (ACI Confidential Containers) [[S:4]]
- Multiple remote code execution (RCE) vulnerabilities were fixed in GitHub Copilot, Visual Studio Code, and Azure SDK [[S:2,4]]
- CISA added all six zero-days to its Known Exploited Vulnerabilities (KEV) catalog [[S:5]]

---

## 2. Wave of Major Data Breaches Across Multiple Sectors [[S:1]]

February 2026 saw a continuation of devastating data breaches that began in January, with attackers using **AI-driven techniques** to launch more sophisticated and stealthy attacks [[S:1]].

### Notable Breaches:

**Government & Public Sector:**
- **Senegal's DAF (Directorate of File Automation)**: **139 TB of data** compromised, including citizen databases, biometric data, immigration records, and backup systems. Operations disrupted for five days [[S:1]]
- **European Commission**: Cyber attack compromised staff personal data including names and mobile numbers; contained within 9 hours [[S:1]]
- **Dutch Data Protection Authority**: Ivanti Endpoint Manager Mobile vulnerability exploited, compromising employee personal information [[S:1]]

**Transportation:**
- **Japan Airlines**: Unauthorized access discovered February 9, 2026, compromising customer data from July 2024 onwards, including names, contact details, and travel information [[S:1]]

**Healthcare:**
- **Terry Reilly Health Services**: Third-party vendor breach exposed patient health insurance and personal health records [[S:1]]
- **San Diego Eye Bank**: Pear ransomware group attack [[S:1]]

**Technology & Services:**
- **Flickr**: Third-party provider breach compromised usernames, IP addresses, location data, and user activity [[S:1]]
- **Substack**: Unauthorized access on February 3, 2026, exposed phone numbers and email addresses [[S:1]]
- **Iron Mountain**: Everest ransomware gang attack compromised internal documents and client personal information [[S:1]]

**Energy & Infrastructure:**
- **Conpet (Romania)**: Qilin ransomware attack compromised over **1 TB** of data including sensitive internal documents, passports, and financial information [[S:1]]

---

## 3. Emerging Cybersecurity Trends Shaping 2026 [[S:3]]

Several major trends are defining the cybersecurity landscape in 2026:

### AI Governance Takes Center Stage [[S:3]]
- Organizations are rapidly adopting AI but lack mature governance frameworks [[S:3]]
- AI risk jumped from **#10 to #2** in business risk concerns according to Allianz Commercial (survey of 3,300+ risk professionals) [[S:3]]
- Growing concerns about AI systems being exploited to exfiltrate corporate data or compromise supply chains [[S:3]]

### Regulatory Shifts [[S:3]]
- Trump administration taking a more nuanced approach to cyber regulation compared to Biden administration [[S:3]]
- SEC dropped landmark civil fraud case against SolarWinds in November 2025, signaling potential shift in enforcement approach [[S:3]]
- Focus moving toward post-breach disclosure rather than pre-incident decision-making investigations [[S:3]]

### Cyber Insurance Evolution [[S:3]]
- Insurers now require phishing-resistant MFA, XDR, and immutable backups for coverage [[S:3]]
- Industry questioning dependence on U.S. market and current premium levels [[S:3]]
- Need for diversification into small-to-midsize business market [[S:3]]

### Operational Resilience Focus [[S:3]]
- Shift from data exfiltration to **operational disruption** as primary attack objective [[S:3]]
- Threat groups like Muddled Libra (Scattered Spider) moving to "deliberate operational sabotage" [[S:3]]
- Examples: Marks & Spencer, Jaguar Land Rover attacks demonstrating supply chain disruption capabilities [[S:3]]

### CVE Program Stabilization [[S:3]]
- Crisis averted after near-collapse of CVE program funding in April 2025 [[S:3]]
- CISA committed to modernizing the program and improving vulnerability data quality [[S:3]]

---

## Summary

February 2026 highlighted the escalating sophistication of cyber threats, with **actively exploited zero-days** requiring immediate patching, **massive data breaches** leveraging AI-enhanced techniques, and a fundamental **shift toward operational disruption** as attackers' primary goal. Organizations are under pressure to mature their AI governance, adapt to evolving regulatory landscapes, and prioritize business resilience alongside traditional security measures.

ACTIVE 💡[ACTIVE SKILLS]
## Skill: pptx-press (public.pptx-press)
# PPTX Authoring for Professional Slide Decks

## Overview
This skill teaches how to produce HTML that renders cleanly into PPTX slides with professional
styling, proper content density, and reliable layouts. Focus: business presentations, technical
decks, and executive briefings.

## Core Principles

### 1. Content Density
Slides auto-scale content down (to ~70% minimum) if it exceeds available space. Always budget
content to fit comfortably within slide dimensions without requiring aggressive scaling.

### 2. Professional Styling
Use domain-appropriate color schemes, clear hierarchy, and balanced layouts. Avoid decorative
elements that don't serve the message.

### 3. Citation Integration
Citations should be concise inline markers `[n]` with full details in a Sources slide, not
disruptive to slide flow.

## HTML Structure

### Slide Container
```html
<section id="slide-1">
  <h1>Slide Title</h1>
  <p class="subtitle">Optional one-line subtitle</p>
  
  <!-- Body content here -->
</section>
```

**CRITICAL REQUIREMENT:**
- **Every slide MUST be wrapped in `<section>` tags** - content outside sections will be silently ignored and won't render
- One `<section>` per slide
- `id` can be any unique identifier
- `<h1>` is the slide title (required for most slides)
- `<p class="subtitle">` for optional subtitle
- All body content goes after title/subtitle

**❌ This will NOT render:**
```html
<body>
  <h1>Title</h1>
  <p>Content...</p>
</body>
```

**✅ This will render:**
```html
<body>
  <section id="slide-1">
    <h1>Title</h1>
    <p>Content...</p>
  </section>
</body>
```

### Supported Body Elements

**Headings:**
```html
<h2>Section Heading</h2>
<h3>Subsection Heading</h3>
```

**Paragraphs:**
```html
<p>Body text with <strong>bold</strong> and <em>italic</em> formatting.</p>
```

**Lists:**
```html
<ul>
  <li><strong>Point:</strong> Short explanation</li>
  <li><strong>Another:</strong> Keep bullets concise</li>
</ul>
```

**Reference Links (for inline citations/sources):**
```html
<div class="reference-link">
  <strong>Climate Action Tracker</strong>
  <a href="https://climateactiontracker.org">Global Emissions Analysis</a>
</div>
```
Use for inline references, documentation links, or resource lists. Each reference-link renders as a separate paragraph with the title in bold followed by the clickable URL.

**Callout Boxes:**
```html
<div class="highlight-box">
  <h3>Key Insight</h3>
  <p>Important information that needs visual emphasis.</p>
</div>
```

**Two-Column Layout:**
```html
<div class="two-column">
  <div class="column">
    <h3>Left Side</h3>
    <ul>
      <li>Point one</li>
      <li>Point two</li>
    </ul>
  </div>
  <div class="column">
    <h3>Right Side</h3>
    <p>Comparison or complementary content.</p>
  </div>
</div>
```

**Tables:**
```html
<table>
  <thead>
    <tr><th>Metric</th><th>Q3</th><th>Q4</th></tr>
  </thead>
  <tbody>
    <tr><td>Revenue</td><td>$2.5M</td><td>$3.1M</td></tr>
  </tbody>
</table>
```

**Images:**
```html
<img src="turn_id/files/chart.png" width="640" alt="Revenue Chart">
<!-- or with inline style -->
<img src="images/diagram.png" style="width:5in; height:3in;" alt="Architecture">
```

## Supported CSS

### Colors (hex only: #RGB or #RRGGBB)
```css
color: #333333;
background: #f0f4f8;
background-color: #0066cc;
```

### Typography
```css
font-size: 18pt;  /* or 1.2em, 16px */
line-height: 1.3; /* number only */
```

### Spacing
```css
padding: 0.2in;
padding-left: 0.3in;
padding-top: 0.1in;
/* Supports: px, pt, in */
```

### Borders (for accents and underlines)
```css
border-bottom: 2px solid #0066cc;  /* Title underline */
border-left: 4px solid #ff6b35;    /* Callout accent */
```

### Two-Column Specific
```css
.two-column { gap: 0.3in; }
.column { 
  background: #f8f9fa; 
  padding: 0.2in;
  border-left: 3px solid #0066cc;
}
```

### Table Styling
```css
th { 
  background-color: #0066cc; 
  color: #ffffff; 
}
tr:nth-child(even) { 
  background-color: #f0f4f8; 
}
```

### Reference Link Styling
```css
.reference-link {
  font-size: 14pt;
  margin-bottom: 0.1in;
  line-height: 1.4;
}
.reference-link strong {
  display: block;
  margin-bottom: 0.03in;
}
.reference-link a {
  color: var(--accent);
  text-decoration: none;
}
```

## DO NOT USE (Ignored by Renderer)

❌ **Layout:**
- `min-height`, `100vh`, `max-height`
- `flex`, `grid` (except implicit in `.two-column`)
- `position: absolute/fixed`
- `page-break-*` properties

❌ **Visual Effects:**
- `box-shadow`, `border-radius`, gradients
- `transform`, `transition`, `animation`
- `opacity` (partial support only)

❌ **Global Resets:**
- `* { ... }` selectors
- Large wrapper divs with generic styling

## Content Budgets (Critical for Proper Fitting)

### Standard Slide
- **1 heading** (h2 or h3)
- **6 short bullets** OR **2 short paragraphs** (~25-40 words each)
- **1 callout box** (~25-40 words)
- Tables: ≤6 columns, ≤8 rows

### Two-Column Slide
- Each column: **1 h3 + 3 bullets** OR **2 short paragraphs**
- Maximum ~12 lines per column
- Keep columns balanced in height

### Tables
- ≤6 columns (wider gets cramped)
- ≤8 rows (taller requires scaling)
- No merged cells
- Keep cell content concise

### Titles & Subtitles
- Title: ≤8 words (one line preferred)
- Subtitle: ≤12 words (one sentence max)

## Professional Color Schemes

### Business/Corporate
```css
:root {
  --primary: #0066cc;      /* IBM Blue */
  --accent: #00a86b;       /* Success Green */
  --text: #333333;         /* Dark Gray */
  --bg-light: #f0f4f8;     /* Light Blue-Gray */
  --bg-callout: #e8f2ff;   /* Soft Blue */
}

h1 { color: var(--primary); border-bottom: 3px solid var(--primary); }
.highlight-box { background: var(--bg-callout); border-left: 4px solid var(--primary); }
th { background-color: var(--primary); color: white; }
```

## Citations

### Inline Citation Format
```html
<p>
  Global EV sales grew ~35% YoY in 2024
  <sup class="cite" data-sids="1,3">[[S:1,3]]</sup>.
</p>
```

**Rules:**
- Add immediately after the factual claim
- `data-sids` contains numeric source IDs (comma-separated or range like 2-4)
- Inner text `[S:...]` must mirror `data-sids`
- Renders as concise `[1] · [3]` with hyperlinks

### Alternative: Footnotes Block
```html
<div class="footnotes">
  <p>Sources: [S:1], [S:3], [S:5]</p>
</div>
```

### Sources Slide
When sources are provided and `include_sources_slide=True`, a final "Sources" slide is
auto-generated with:
- [n] Title (domain)
- Clickable hyperlinks to sources

## Complete Slide Templates

### Template 1: Executive Summary
```html
<section id="slide-1">
  <h1>Executive Summary</h1>
  <p class="subtitle">Q4 2025 Performance Highlights</p>
  
  <h2>Key Achievements</h2>
  <ul>
    <li><strong>Revenue:</strong> $3.2M (+28% YoY)</li>
    <li><strong>Growth:</strong> 450 new customers</li>
    <li><strong>Efficiency:</strong> 35% cost reduction</li>
  </ul>
  
  <div class="highlight-box">
    <h3>Strategic Priority</h3>
    <p>Expand into EMEA market Q1 2026 with localized offerings.</p>
  </div>
</section>
```

### Template 2: Data Comparison (Two-Column)
```html
<section id="slide-2">
  <h1>Market Analysis</h1>
  
  <div class="two-column">
    <div class="column">
      <h3>Opportunities</h3>

  </div>
</section>
```

```html
</section>
```

```html

  <h1>Market Trends</h1>

  <p>
    Global EV sales reached 14M units in 2024, representing ~18% of total 
    auto sales <sup class="cite" data-sids="1">[[S:1]]</sup>. Growth is 
    accelerated by policy incentives and falling battery costs 
    <sup class="cite" data-sids="2,3">[[S:2,3]]</sup>.
  </p>
</section>
```

### Template 5: Reference Links in Columns
```html

  <h1>Research Methodology</h1>
  <p class="subtitle">Data sources and analysis framework</p>
  
  <div class="two-column">
    <div class="column">
      <h3>Primary Data Sources</h3>
      <div class="reference-link">
        <strong>World Bank Open Data</strong>
        <a href="https://data.worldbank.org">Economic Indicators Database</a>
      </div>
      <div class="reference-link">
        <strong>OECD Statistics</strong>
        <a href="https://stats.oecd.org">International Comparisons</a>
      </div>
      <div class="reference-link">
        <strong>UN Population Division</strong>
        <a href="https://population.un.org/wpp">Demographic Projections</a>
      </div>
    </div>
    <div class="column">
      <h3>Analysis Timeline</h3>
      <ul>
        <li><strong>Data Collection (Weeks 1-3):</strong> Gather datasets, validate sources</li>
        <li><strong>Processing (Weeks 4-6):</strong> Clean data, run initial models</li>
        <li><strong>Validation (Weeks 7-9):</strong> Peer review, sensitivity analysis</li>
      </ul>
    </div>
  </div>
</section>
```

## Common Mistakes to Avoid

### ❌ Missing Section Tags (CRITICAL)
```html
<!-- BAD: Content will be silently ignored -->
<body>
  <h1>My Presentation</h1>
  <h2>Section 1</h2>
  <p>Content here...</p>
</body>
```
**Fix:** Wrap ALL content in `<section>` tags. Each section = one slide.
```html
<!-- GOOD: Content will render -->
<body>
  <section id="slide-1">
    <h1>My Presentation</h1>
    <h2>Section 1</h2>
    <p>Content here...</p>
  </section>
</body>
```

### ❌ Content Overload
```html
<!-- BAD: 12 bullets won't fit -->
<ul>
  <li>Point 1 with very long explanation...</li>
  <li>Point 2 with even more text...</li>
  <!-- 10 more bullets -->
</ul>
```
**Fix:** Split into 2-3 slides with 4-6 bullets each.

### ❌ Tiny Columns
```html
<!-- BAD: Each column has 8 bullets -->
<div class="two-column">
  <div class="column">
    <ul><li>...</li><!-- 8 items --></ul>
  </div>
  <div class="column">
    <ul><li>...</li><!-- 8 items --></ul>
  </div>
</div>
```
**Fix:** Max 3-4 bullets per column.

### ❌ Unsupported CSS
```html
<style>
/* BAD: These are ignored */
.box { 
  box-shadow: 0 2px 8px rgba(0,0,0,0.1); 
  border-radius: 8px;
  transform: scale(1.1);
}
</style>
```
**Fix:** Use only supported properties.

### ❌ Base64 Images
```html
<!-- BAD: Will trigger warning -->
<img src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KG...">
```
**Fix:** Use file paths: `<img src="turn_id/files/chart.png">`

### ❌ Long Titles
```html
<!-- BAD: Title wraps to 3 lines -->
<h1>Comprehensive Analysis of Q4 2025 Financial Performance and Strategic Market Positioning</h1>
```
**Fix:** `<h1>Q4 2025 Financial Performance</h1>` (use subtitle for details)

## Professional Practices

### 1. Visual Hierarchy
```html
<style>
h1 { font-size: 36pt; color: var(--primary); }
h2 { font-size: 28pt; color: var(--primary); margin-top: 0.2in; }
h3 { font-size: 22pt; color: var(--text); }
p { font-size: 18pt; line-height: 1.3; }
</style>
```

### 2. Balanced Layouts
- Single-column: Center-aligned, clear hierarchy
- Two-column: Equal visual weight, related content
- Mixed: Vary layouts between slides for visual interest

### 3. Callout Usage
Use callouts for:
- Key takeaways
- Action items
- Important warnings
- Strategic priorities

Avoid:
- Decorative boxes with no purpose
- Multiple callouts per slide (use max 1-2)

### 4. Color Consistency
- Stick to 2-3 colors per deck (primary + accent + neutrals)
- Use primary for headings and key elements
- Use accent sparingly for emphasis
- Keep backgrounds light for readability

### 5. Reference Links vs Citations
**Use `<div class="reference-link">` when:**
- Listing authoritative sources/standards (data sources, documentation, reports)
- Building a resource/bibliography section
- Links are the primary content

**Use `<sup class="cite">` when:**
- Citing specific facts inline
- Supporting claims with evidence
- Links are secondary to narrative flow

## Image Guidelines

### File Paths (Required)
```html
<!-- Relative from OUT_DIR -->
<img src="turn_id/files/revenue_chart.png" width="640">

<!-- With explicit dimensions -->
<img src="images/architecture.png" style="width:6in; height:4in;">
```

### Sizing
- Specify width OR width+height
- Use inches for print consistency: `width:5in; height:3in;`
- Use pixels for web-friendly: `width="640"` (converts to ~6.7in at 96dpi)
- Images auto-fit to slide width if too large

### Placement
- Top-level images appear below title
- Images in columns appear inline with column content
- Images in callouts appear inside the callout box

## Performance Tips

1. **Keep HTML compact** - Remove unnecessary whitespace
2. **Minimize CSS** - Define common colors as variables, reuse classes
3. **Consolidate slides** - Don't split content unnecessarily
4. **Test content density** - If unsure, err on less content per slide

## Remember
- **CRITICAL: Wrap all content in `<section>` tags** - one section per slide, content outside sections won't render
- Content auto-scales down (min 70%) if too large - avoid this by budgeting properly
- Renderer measures text to determine fit - longer text = more scaling
- Citations render as `[n]` inline - keep factual claims concise
- Sources slide is auto-generated - don't create manually
- Two-column backgrounds/borders are per-column - style individually
- Reference links create clickable paragraph elements - use for resource lists

# Top 3 Cybersecurity News Stories in February 2026

## 1. Microsoft Patch Tuesday: 54 Vulnerabilities Fixed Including 6 Actively Exploited Zero-Days [[S:2,4,5]]

On **February 10, 2026**, Microsoft released its Patch Tuesday updates addressing **54 vulnerabilities** across Windows, Office, Azure, and developer tools. The most critical aspect of this update was the patching of **six zero-day vulnerabilities** that were actively being exploited in the wild [[S:4,5]].

### The Six Zero-Days:
- **CVE-2026-21510**: Windows Shell security feature bypass allowing attackers to execute code via malicious links [[S:5]]
- **CVE-2026-21514**: Microsoft Office Word security bypass enabling OLE mitigation bypass [[S:4,5]]
- **CVE-2026-21513**: MSHTML Framework (Internet Explorer) security bypass [[S:4,5]]
- **CVE-2026-21519**: Desktop Window Manager elevation of privilege vulnerability [[S:4,5]]
- **CVE-2026-21533**: Windows Remote Desktop Services privilege escalation to SYSTEM level [[S:4,5]]
- **CVE-2026-21525**: Windows Remote Access Connection Manager denial-of-service [[S:4,5]]

### Key Details:
- Google Threat Intelligence Group (GTIG) was credited with discovering several of these vulnerabilities, suggesting possible nation-state or commercial spyware vendor involvement [[S:5]]
- CrowdStrike discovered CVE-2026-21533, noting that the exploit modifies service configuration keys to enable privilege escalation [[S:5]]
- Two **Critical** severity vulnerabilities were also patched in Azure Compute Gallery (ACI Confidential Containers) [[S:4]]
- Multiple remote code execution (RCE) vulnerabilities were fixed in GitHub Copilot, Visual Studio Code, and Azure SDK [[S:2,4]]
- CISA added all six zero-days to its Known Exploited Vulnerabilities (KEV) catalog [[S:5]]

---

## 2. Wave of Major Data Breaches Across Multiple Sectors [[S:1]]

February 2026 saw a continuation of devastating data breaches that began in January, with attackers using **AI-driven techniques** to launch more sophisticated and stealthy attacks [[S:1]].

### Notable Breaches:

**Government & Public Sector:**
- **Senegal's DAF (Directorate of File Automation)**: **139 TB of data** compromised, including citizen databases, biometric data, immigration records, and backup systems. Operations disrupted for five days [[S:1]]
- **European Commission**: Cyber attack compromised staff personal data including names and mobile numbers; contained within 9 hours [[S:1]]
- **Dutch Data Protection Authority**: Ivanti Endpoint Manager Mobile vulnerability exploited, compromising employee personal information [[S:1]]

**Transportation:**
- **Japan Airlines**: Unauthorized access discovered February 9, 2026, compromising customer data from July 2024 onwards, including names, contact details, and travel information [[S:1]]

**Healthcare:**
- **Terry Reilly Health Services**: Third-party vendor breach exposed patient health insurance and personal health records [[S:1]]
- **San Diego Eye Bank**: Pear ransomware group attack [[S:1]]

**Technology & Services:**
- **Flickr**: Third-party provider breach compromised usernames, IP addresses, location data, and user activity [[S:1]]
- **Substack**: Unauthorized access on February 3, 2026, exposed phone numbers and email addresses [[S:1]]
- **Iron Mountain**: Everest ransomware gang attack compromised internal documents and client personal information [[S:1]]

**Energy & Infrastructure:**
- **Conpet (Romania)**: Qilin ransomware attack compromised over **1 TB** of data including sensitive internal documents, passports, and financial information [[S:1]]

---

## 3. Emerging Cybersecurity Trends Shaping 2026 [[S:3]]

Several major trends are defining the cybersecurity landscape in 2026:

### AI Governance Takes Center Stage [[S:3]]
- Organizations are rapidly adopting AI but lack mature governance frameworks [[S:3]]
- AI risk jumped from **#10 to #2** in business risk concerns according to Allianz Commercial (survey of 3,300+ risk professionals) [[S:3]]
- Growing concerns about AI systems being exploited to exfiltrate corporate data or compromise supply chains [[S:3]]

### Regulatory Shifts [[S:3]]
- Trump administration taking a more nuanced approach to cyber regulation compared to Biden administration [[S:3]]
- SEC dropped landmark civil fraud case against SolarWinds in November 2025, signaling potential shift in enforcement approach [[S:3]]
- Focus moving toward post-breach disclosure rather than pre-incident decision-making investigations [[S:3]]

### Cyber Insurance Evolution [[S:3]]
- Insurers now require phishing-resistant MFA, XDR, and immutable backups for coverage [[S:3]]
- Industry questioning dependence on U.S. market and current premium levels [[S:3]]
- Need for diversification into small-to-midsize business market [[S:3]]

### Operational Resilience Focus [[S:3]]
- Shift from data exfiltration to **operational disruption** as primary attack objective [[S:3]]
- Threat groups like Muddled Libra (Scattered Spider) moving to "deliberate operational sabotage" [[S:3]]
- Examples: Marks & Spencer, Jaguar Land Rover attacks demonstrating supply chain disruption capabilities [[S:3]]

### CVE Program Stabilization [[S:3]]
- Crisis averted after near-collapse of CVE program funding in April 2025 [[S:3]]
- CISA committed to modernizing the program and improving vulnerability data quality [[S:3]]

---

## Summary

February 2026 highlighted the escalating sophistication of cyber threats, with **actively exploited zero-days** requiring immediate patching, **massive data breaches** leveraging AI-enhanced techniques, and a fundamental **shift toward operational disruption** as attackers' primary goal. Organizations are under pressure to mature their AI governance, adapt to evolving regulatory landscapes, and prioritize business resilience alongside traditional security measures.
